It is trans. immediately, and by means of the prep. <foreign lang="ar">ب</foreign>; (L, Msb, K;) but some say that the <foreign lang="ar">ب</foreign> is redundant in this case; and most of the lexicologists disallow it with this form of the verb, allowing it only with <foreign lang="ar">أَوْعَدَ</foreign>. (TA.) It is also used with reference to good and evil: (S, L, Msb, K:) you say <foreign lang="ar">وَعَدَهُ خَيْرًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He promised him good</hi>]: and <foreign lang="ar">وَعَدَهُ شَرًّا</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He threatened him with evil</hi>]: (Fr, Fs, S, L, Msb, K, &amp;c.:) and, [accord. to some,] <foreign lang="ar">وعده بِخَيْرٍ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">بِشَرّ</foreign>. (IKoot, Msb.) When neither good nor evil is mentioned, if you mean the former, you say <foreign lang="ar">وَعَدَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He promised good</hi>]: and if you mean the latter,

                     <L>

A saying of the Arabs.
